Radiometric errors occur since\nthe MTF falls off as the size of an object in\nthe scene decreases The decreased modulation\nmeans that \tthe image of the object will have\nlesser or greater density than the image of the\nsame type of object in a larger size.\n\nColor prints have a gamma close to 2 and a\ntonal range that allows 14 of the 15 gray\nsteps to be discerned. Current practice in the\nphotographic facility for products that do not\ncover a 2.0 density range is to expose them\nso that saturation occurs at the second darkest\nstep of the gray scale.\nH.2.3.2 Modulation Transfer Function\n\nThe MTF of the 70mm third generation\npositive is given in Figure H-26. The response\n\nModulation Transfer Function (MTF) is the\nresponse to a sine wave at frequency f after\nimage processing relative to the amplitude of\nthe sine wave previous to processing\n\nThe\n\nMTF of the PPS is determined by contact\nprinting a sine wave target onto film, proces\xc2\xad\nsing, and then measuring the transmission of\nthe film using a microdensitometer.\nThe sine wave target is a film transparency\nthat has transmission varying sinusoidally as\na function of distance The target contains\nfrequencies including the rarge from 1.5 to\n42 cycles per mm. The modulation of the\n\n.\n\ntarget equals-\n\nFigure H-26. \tSine Wave Response, Third Generation\n70 MM\n\nTmax - Tmin\n\nTmax + Tmin\n\nis relatively flat over the frequency range. At\n40 cycles per mm the photographic system\nMTF is about four times the sensor MTF and\nthus is not the limiting factor in resolving\npower or radiometric errors For enlarged\nproducts the photographic system MTF has\neven less effect because of the larger format,\nhowever, the enlarger MTF must be consider\xc2\xad\ned. Tests of the enlarger MTF indicate its\nresponse to be about 2.5 times that of the sen\xc2\xad\nsors at 40 cycles per mm Thus the photogra\xc2\xad\nphic system MTF will have little effect on 9.5\xc2\xad\ninch products\n\nwhere Tmax and Tmin are the transmissions\nat the peak of the sine wave. The target\nmodulation is 0.6. This modulation is measured using the same microdensitometer as\nthe film being tested and the reported modulation divided by the target modulation. The\nphotographic system MTF includes the effect\nof printers in addition to the film emulsion.\nMTF is measured using a macrodensitometer\nhaving a slit of small width and large height\n\nk+-21I\n\nH.2.3.3 Granularity\n\nThe film noise increases five to\'six times in\ngoing from the first to the third generation\nand is approximately inversely proportional\'\nto the aperture diameter within afilm genera\xc2\xad\ntion.\n\nFilm granularity is the rms density variation\nabout a mean density level as measured with\naspecified microdensitometer aperture. Granularity isthe integrated film noise from a spatia\xc2\xad\nfrequency close to zero up to a frequency\ncorresponding to the diameter of the scanning\naperture. Very low frequency noise isremoved\nfrom the granularity measurements and reported separately as spatial non-uniformity,\nGranularity is given as 1000 times the measured value.\n\nH.2.3.4 Spatial Uniformity\nSpatial non-uniformity is the rms variation in\ndensity over the image area of the processed\nfilm exposed with a uniform level of gray\nSpatiaI non-uniformity introduces an error in\nrelating density measurements within the\nimage or between points in the image and the\nannotation gray scale.\n\nIn a single photographic generation, granularity increases in proportion to the square\nroot of density, but this proportionality does\nnot apply in a multi-generation photo system\nHigh granularity in the first generation results\nin a low granularity in the second generation\nbecause of the density reversal in going from a\npositive to a negative Also, the resultant\ngranularity is a function of the MTF of\nprinters and emulsion and the gradient of the\ndensity-log exposure curve,\n\nSpatial uniformity is measured using a densitometer with a 1 mm aperture on 70mm film\nand a 3mm aperture on 95-inch film. The\nfilm is exposed using a point light source\nto obtain uniform exposure After processing\nto the appropriate generation, density mea\xc2\xad\nsurements are made over the image area and\nthe rms value computed\nGiven spatial non-uniformity measured in\ndensity units, the transmission error\nisAT\n\nAD (T)\n0434\n\n0where,\n\n-\n\n4\n\n.<x/\n\nAD = Spatial non-uniformity\nT\n0_\n\nX\n\n~\n\n= Transmission- level, percent\n\nSpatial uniformity tests have been made for\n70mm third generation and enlarged 9 5-\n\nX\n\nX\n\nx\n\n12APERTURE\n4\n\ninch third generation transparencies Typical-\n\nFORENERATION\nR-\n\n--\n\nWEboth\n\n04 to 0 08 for 70mm\nproducts and from 0006 to 0.10 for 9.5-inch\n\nly AD ranges from\n\nTHD ENEATION\n\nproducts including the effects of the enlarger.\nH.2.4 Dimensional Stability\n\n6E.SaY U.IT\n\nFigure H-27.
